  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_02301456-39f1-41df-a4af-1e9fb2bcbce1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/570631-can-you-jump-in-at-any-book-for-dresden">Can you jump in at any book for Dresden Files books or are you supposed to start with #1?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_570631'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F3475161-turn-coat">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/21210066-john"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1370945913i/21210066._UX100_CR0,1,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/21210066-john">John</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I was thinking about this today and then saw your question. I've started reading from book one, and there is a progression. You can start from any boo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I was thinking about this today and then saw your question. I've started reading from book one, and there is a progression. You can start from any book you wish, but beware that there are references to earlier books with a bit of emphasis on the one directly previous to. It's a chain, you can start in the middle but you'd be missing out on the beginning. One thing to note though. The last ones in the series are very good whereas some of the first ones can be a little hit and miss. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_3091106121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3091106121" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3091106121?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6416196-turn-coat">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3091106121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12322632007482762570"><b>4.5/5 stars<br/><br/><i>Turn Coat</i> is one of my favorite volume in the series so far, it’s up there with <i>Dead Beat</i> and <i>White Night</i>.</b><br/><br/>We can’t always win. That’s what life is. There are moments of glory, happiness, and there are times when we will lose, faces pain, and hopefully rises up then move on from it. Turn Coat is the eleventh volume in The Dresden Files by Jim Butcher, and it hammered these themes into the readers incredibly well. There has always been a rumor of a traitor in the white council, and this</span>
  <span id="freeText12322632007482762570" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 stars<br><br><i>Turn Coat</i> is one of my favorite volume in the series so far, it’s up there with <i>Dead Beat</i> and <i>White Night</i>.</b><br><br>We can’t always win. That’s what life is. There are moments of glory, happiness, and there are times when we will lose, faces pain, and hopefully rises up then move on from it. Turn Coat is the eleventh volume in The Dresden Files by Jim Butcher, and it hammered these themes into the readers incredibly well. There has always been a rumor of a traitor in the white council, and this book narrowed the focus of the story on this as it begins with Morgan asking Harry Dresden for help because he’s accused of a murder he didn’t commit. There isn’t much to say on this review; this is the usual high standard of the series, Butcher utilizes murder-mystery whodunit storytelling with themes that evocatively put and relatable.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“There are bad things in the world. There's no getting away from that. But that doesn't mean nothing can be done about them. You can't abandon life just because it's scary, and just because sometimes you get hurt. ”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Harry Dresden may not be an encompassingly good-hearted character, but that’s what it means to be a human right? No one is perfect, after all. I do, however, found myself impressed by Harry’s decision to help Morgan. If you’ve been following the series, we know that Harry and Morgan have issues with each other; they both pretty much hated each other’s guts to the core. But Harry, despite his feelings towards Morgan, still decided to help him because he knows it’s the right thing to do, and that’s something praise-worthy; helping someone you don’t like, or hate, isn’t an easy act to do. It was so great seeing how much further Harry’s relationship with Murphy, Thomas, Molly, and of course, Mouse developed here.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“The human mind isn't a terribly logical or consistent place. Most people, given the choice to face a hideous or terrifying truth or to conveniently avoid it, choose the convenience and peace of normality. That doesn't make them strong or weak people, or good or bad people. It just makes them people.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I’m being repetitive again, but yeah, as always for this series, the longevity of the action sequences hurt the pacing slightly for me. Not saying it wasn’t good, my interest and concentration just wandered easily when the action scenes in any book of the series so far went on a bit too long. Thankfully, there was only one big action sequence—usually there were two—and what came after the part with Demonreach was freaking incredible. Seriously, the last two or three chapters were filled with intensity and a new level of seriousness that was missing from the previous books.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“No one is an unjust villain in his own mind. Even - perhaps even especially - those who are the worst of us. Some of the cruelest tyrants in history were motivated by noble ideals, or made choices that they would call 'hard but necessary steps' for the good of their nation. We're all the hero of our own story.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Amid the well-written murder-mystery, <i>Turn Coat</i> also teaches us about the necessity of pain, hardship, and moving on in our life. Eleven books in, and it terrifies me how Butcher maintained the great quality of each book in the series since the fourth installment so consistently. I haven’t rated any books in the series with a below 4-stars rating since <i>Summer Knight</i>. Will there be any… <i>CHANGES</i> (Hahahaha!) in the next book, though? The next book in the series has often been praised as the best book of the entire series so far, and I’m very much excited to find out why.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“See, here’s the thing. Morgan was right: you can’t win them all. But that doesn’t mean that you give up. Not ever.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>Picture: <i>Turn Coat</i> by Vincent Chong</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596620562i/29918566._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780356500379/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><b>You can find <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2020/08/05/book-review-turn-coat-the-dresden-files-11-by-jim-butcher/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u> and the rest of my reviews at <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b><br><br><i>Special thanks to my Patrons on <b><u><a href="https://www.patreon.com/petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Patreon</a></u></b> for giving me extra support towards my passion for reading and reviewing!<br><br>My Patrons: Alfred, Alya, Annabeth, Devin, Hamad, Jimmy Nutts, Joie, Mike, Miracle, Nicholas, Zoe.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12322632007482762570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9204440834572762823">I often have a difficult time reviewing books in a series, so I'll just say this one thing: I'm continually thrilled by the fact that every event in the Dresden Files series is relevant to the struggle in Turn Coat. So many authors miss the "why?" - why start a series at a certain point in time? Why is the main character the focal point, how are they special? Why does anything happen? Jim Butcher has an answer for each question and I want to hug him for it. Once again, he serves up sacrifices an</span>
  <span id="freeText9204440834572762823" style="display:none">I often have a difficult time reviewing books in a series, so I'll just say this one thing: I'm continually thrilled by the fact that every event in the Dresden Files series is relevant to the struggle in Turn Coat. So many authors miss the "why?" - why start a series at a certain point in time? Why is the main character the focal point, how are they special? Why does anything happen? Jim Butcher has an answer for each question and I want to hug him for it. Once again, he serves up sacrifices and tough blows along with the victories, and it's become clear to me that Butcher and Joss Whedon have a lot in common.<br /><br />Okay, when's the next book coming out? :)</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1334317033" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1334317033?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-mystery">paranormal-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1334317033" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8950360285685477335">Another question for my non-southern friends: is it really a problem for you if a man opens a door for you? Because Harry keeps saying that he's a chauvinist for doing things like opening doors for women, and that Murphy gets mad when he does it for her, but that's just crazy talk to me. Crazy talk! Because, here in Texas, where I live, a man is <b>expected</b> to open a door for a woman. It doesn't matter what age either the male or female is, or the health of either. If you have a penis, you are the </span>
  <span id="freeText8950360285685477335" style="display:none">Another question for my non-southern friends: is it really a problem for you if a man opens a door for you? Because Harry keeps saying that he's a chauvinist for doing things like opening doors for women, and that Murphy gets mad when he does it for her, but that's just crazy talk to me. Crazy talk! Because, here in Texas, where I live, a man is <b>expected</b> to open a door for a woman. It doesn't matter what age either the male or female is, or the health of either. If you have a penis, you are the designated door-opener. I don't care if the guy is blind with only one leg. He'd better hobble on over to where he thinks that door is if he smells the scent of a woman's perfume. It's his duty. I haven't opened a door for myself in 18 years. I don't think I know how to do it anymore. If I'm out alone, I have to just stand there in front of an establishment until a nice man comes along and opens it for me. Thank the good Lord for strong men! Bless their hearts!<br><br>As I have said before, Harry would fit in well here. Hmm, except for the godless thing. We'd all have to pray for his pagan soul. But, other than that...<br><br>On to the book!<br>So, I have been hoping that things would change a little in the Harry Dresden formula. You know, the "Harry gets a case, Harry fights the scary monsters and wins, Harry solves the case" thing? Like Scooby Doo. And, it looks like we might be heading that way. Because things didn't go so well for Harry this time. There are also some things that could be foreshadows of future bad things.<br><br><b>
  <i>They'd been a problem, the past several months - increasingly painful migraines.</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/what%20does%20it%20mean" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436996902ra/15526908.gif" alt="what does it mean photo: Community- What Does that Mean Jeff_WhatDoesThatMean_zpsc6f8dab6.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>it doesn't just mean he needs more aspirin!</i><br><br>Harry's main goal in this book is to find the killer of one of the members of the White Council, which is the wizard's senate. And, yes, they are about as effective, corrupt, and out-of-touch as our politicians. Oh, and hundreds of years old - like our politicians. <br><br>The main suspect in the murder is Harry's old nemesis, Morgan - the guy who has wanted to kill him since he was 16. It is Harry's perfect chance for revenge! Now, Morgan has the death sentence. Harry can sit back and let heads roll (Morgan's head, that is). But, Harry is a boy scout and can't let Morgan take the fall because he's innocent. What a softie! So, he is helping Morgan and trying to find the real killer. <br><br>Things get complicated real fast. And, surprisingly, things get dark in this book. People die - people that we have gotten to know and like. And, things don't end well. At all.<br><br>I'm glad to see this departure from the usual Harry Dresden formula, although there were some sad moments. I can't wait to find out where this goes next.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2583467198" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2583467198?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fantasy-and-sci-fi">fantasy-and-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2583467198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10177864725657459761">For once, Harry Dresden was minding his own business when trouble showed up at his doorstep. Morgan, one of the wardens of the White Council who has hounded Harry for nearly his entire life, needs saving... from the wardens of the White Council. Oh how the mighty have fallen.<br/><br/>Why would Harry stick his neck out for one of the few men on the planet who has never liked him?<br/><br/><i>"Because Morgan wouldn't break the Laws of Magic," I said quietly. "Not even if it cost him his life."</i> pg 19, ebook.<br/><br/>Something st</span>
  <span id="freeText10177864725657459761" style="display:none">For once, Harry Dresden was minding his own business when trouble showed up at his doorstep. Morgan, one of the wardens of the White Council who has hounded Harry for nearly his entire life, needs saving... from the wardens of the White Council. Oh how the mighty have fallen.<br /><br />Why would Harry stick his neck out for one of the few men on the planet who has never liked him?<br /><br /><i>"Because Morgan wouldn't break the Laws of Magic," I said quietly. "Not even if it cost him his life."</i> pg 19, ebook.<br /><br />Something strange is going on and, as usual, Harry's going to get to the bottom of it. But, this time, the solution comes at great personal cost and Harry's life may never be the same.<br /><br />Excellent entry in the Dresden Files which, despite concerns that after 11 books it may have become repetitive or go off the rails, continues to impress. Jim Butcher seems to have found a sweet spot between bringing in old characters and plot lines while introducing new twists. It is an urban fantasy reader's treat.<br /><br /><i>There are bad things in the world. There's no getting away from that. But that doesn't mean nothing can be done about them. You can't abandon life just because it's scary, and just because sometimes you get hurt."</i> pg 45, ebook.<br /><br />The lines between good and evil are truly becoming blurred as the White Council continues to be assaulted from the outside. As a reader, I thought of the wizards of the highest council as unassailable gods, but in <i>Turn Coat</i>, they are revealed to be as human as the next person. They can be confused, manipulated and used for other ends. <br /><br />Harry's sardonic humor is in evidence throughout this tale, delivering his one-liners with his usual flair: <i>"They always have good coffee here," Ebenezar said a few moments later. "And they don't call it funny names," I said. "It's just coffee. Not frappalattegrandechino."</i> pg 138<br /><br />But as the story lines get darker, I can't help but wonder how much more Harry can take before he snaps. Or the bad guys finally win the day.<br /><br /><i>"Everyone dies, honey," I said, very quietly. "Everyone. There's no 'if.' There's only 'when.'... When you die, do you want to feel ashamed of what you've done with your life? Feel ashamed of what your life meant?"</i> pg 338, ebook.<br /><br />Highly recommended for fantasy fans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10177864725657459761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1085280816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085280816" />
    <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda"><img alt="Arah-Lynda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601299926p2/5859453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085280816?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arah-Lynda" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda">Arah-Lynda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5859453-arah-lynda?shelf=i-said">i-said</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085280816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2065277925256753215">In absolute fairness my reading of this novel suffered from two things.<br/><br/>First and foremost this is the only Harry Dresden novel I have ever read. While enjoyable I am certain that I would have benefitted greatly in knowing more about Dresden’s world from the earlier novels in the series. <br/><br/>Secondly, I started this right on the heels of having read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/745634.On_South_Mountain_The_Dark_Secrets_Of_The_Goler_Clan' title='On South Mountain The Dark Secrets Of The Goler Clan by David Cruise' rel='nofollow noopener'>On South Mountain: The Dark Secrets Of The Goler Clan</a> a vile true account of what life was like for the children of the Goler Clan of Nova Scotia. It has</span>
  <span id="freeText2065277925256753215" style="display:none">In absolute fairness my reading of this novel suffered from two things.<br /><br />First and foremost this is the only Harry Dresden novel I have ever read. While enjoyable I am certain that I would have benefitted greatly in knowing more about Dresden’s world from the earlier novels in the series. <br /><br />Secondly, I started this right on the heels of having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/745634.On_South_Mountain_The_Dark_Secrets_Of_The_Goler_Clan" title="On South Mountain The Dark Secrets Of The Goler Clan by David Cruise" rel="nofollow noopener">On South Mountain: The Dark Secrets Of The Goler Clan</a> a vile true account of what life was like for the children of the Goler Clan of Nova Scotia. It has seeped into my pores and wreaks havoc on my soul even now.<br /><br />That said, it seems to me that Jim Butcher has a winning series going on here and some day I hope to visit the earliest novel in the series and gain some much warranted background.<br /><br />My favourite sequence in this offering was the battle between Injun Joe and the naagloshii. Loved it, oh and Toot-toot too.<br /><br />3.5 stars which I am sure would be a certain 4 for a seasoned Dresden reader.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2065277925256753215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4841820324722928845"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>The last several books in <i>The Dresden Files</i> had been really, <i>really</i> good. <i>Turn Coat</i> has got to be one of the more emotional instalments of the series so far.   <span id="freeText4841820324722928845" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br /><br />The last several books in <i>The Dresden Files</i> had been really, <i>really</i> good. <i>Turn Coat</i> has got to be one of the more emotional instalments of the series so far. The only way this could have been achieved was due to the fantastic character development of the main cast which to me started somewhere around the fifth book, which was my favourite title up till then. Someone whom I used to dislike, and still did for pretty much a large part of this book, completely took me by surprise in a most poignant manner which resulted in an emotionally powerful ending. Finally, the second to last scene left me in a world of hurt. I'm worried for my heart as I progress to the next book, <i>Changes</i>, in the near future.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer5713266095100467168">Things are getting pretty serious in the Dresden Files as Harry hunts down a traitor in the White Council of wizards. When Morgan, the warden who once wanted to kill Harry, turns up on his doorstep hurt and on the run from the White Council Harry knows something is seriously wrong as Morgan has been accused of a crime Harry knows he would never commit. The White Court of vampires have also been set up by someone in their ranks and form an uneasy truce with Harry and the wardens to flush out the </span>
  <span id="freeText5713266095100467168" style="display:none">Things are getting pretty serious in the Dresden Files as Harry hunts down a traitor in the White Council of wizards. When Morgan, the warden who once wanted to kill Harry, turns up on his doorstep hurt and on the run from the White Council Harry knows something is seriously wrong as Morgan has been accused of a crime Harry knows he would never commit. The White Court of vampires have also been set up by someone in their ranks and form an uneasy truce with Harry and the wardens to flush out the traitors. <br /><br />Still plenty of fun and wisecracks from Harry in this episode as he sets about looking for the dark forces at work. He is also being hunted by a large, scary shapeshifter from Indian mythology and must use some ingenious magic to escape and protect those around him. No significant new characters in this one, although we do get to learn a lot more about some of the other wardens and their magical talents and get to see their headquarters in Edinburgh. Harry not only takes some heavy physical hits in this episode but also some heavy personal ones. An entertaining episode moving the plot along to the war that is sure to resume between the wizards and the red vampires. </span>

<div id="review_52177558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52177558" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1282558-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1214790635p2/1282558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52177558?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/1282558-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1282558-rebecca?shelf=modern-earth">modern-earth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1282558-rebecca?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52177558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13433691980564420991">This time Harry Dresden, Wizard detective, is trying to find the traitor in the White Council, after Morgan shows up on his doorstep on the lam for a crime he didn't commit and Harry realized that hes got to either turn Morgan in or help him out (and get blamed for helping a criminal).<br/><br/>The good things:<br/>-- We get to see more of the White Council, find out more about Morgan, Luccio and Listen-to-Wind. We also see a bit of why the Council thinks about Harry the way they do, and some awesome magic. <br/>--</span>
  <span id="freeText13433691980564420991" style="display:none">This time Harry Dresden, Wizard detective, is trying to find the traitor in the White Council, after Morgan shows up on his doorstep on the lam for a crime he didn't commit and Harry realized that hes got to either turn Morgan in or help him out (and get blamed for helping a criminal).<br /><br />The good things:<br />-- We get to see more of the White Council, find out more about Morgan, Luccio and Listen-to-Wind. We also see a bit of why the Council thinks about Harry the way they do, and some awesome magic. <br />-- I once read a maxim about how authors are willing to make characters struggle for what they need (read: plot) but are willing to give in on things that the characters want but don't need. Not to spoil things, but Jim Butcher doesn't do that in this book. Harry might solve the mystery, but he gets dealt several nasty punches for it -- it's definitely bittersweet. <br />-- The banter is good, and I always appreciate that most characters can keep up with Harry verbally. It's nice to see that Harry doesn't get all the good lines. <br /><br />The bad things:<br />-- The traitor's plot is clever, but the identity of the traitor was a bit of a let down. A friend compared it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire__Book_4_" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (Book 4) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a>, when a giant deal was made about a character dying, when you find out that the character was only a minor character until that book. That and I kind of pegged it -- partly because my friend told me this beforehand, maybe. <br /><br />Plus, Mouse totally stole the show. Mouse is awesome. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13433691980564420991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6416196-turn-coat">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3225938726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3604898350690958429">Full Video Review Here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/f20fYDLyvhI'>https://youtu.be/f20fYDLyvhI</a><br/><br/>What I knew about Turn Coat before I started is that it was the book that came before Changes. That's it. But it turned out to be so much more than that. Like Small Favor, this one continued the hiccup I had with White Night. With one of the best baddies in the series so far in the Skinwalker as well as an unlikely alliance, the fun never stops even when the stakes are high as ever.<br/><br/>Personally, I've been waiting for Morgan to have a bigger part </span>
  <span id="freeText3604898350690958429" style="display:none">Full Video Review Here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/f20fYDLyvhI">https://youtu.be/f20fYDLyvhI</a><br /><br />What I knew about Turn Coat before I started is that it was the book that came before Changes. That's it. But it turned out to be so much more than that. Like Small Favor, this one continued the hiccup I had with White Night. With one of the best baddies in the series so far in the Skinwalker as well as an unlikely alliance, the fun never stops even when the stakes are high as ever.<br /><br />Personally, I've been waiting for Morgan to have a bigger part in these books and it happens here. We also have growth for recurring characters that is much needed. But not just the big ones; yes Molly and Thomas get even more depth here, but smaller characters like Billy and Toot-Toot get good moments and character development.<br /><br />The amazing thing is that Butcher has been able to keep this series so fresh through 11 books. I'm not in the "each book is better than the last one" camp that many Dresdenphiles are, but I can see why they say that because after this many books almost none of it seems filler.<br /><br />If you want the punchin', it's there. If you want character moments, they're there. If you need levity in the face of all the high stakes, yes, it is there. Butcher is just showing off at this point and I'm so glad to be along for the ride.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14352740202561895577"><b>Turn Coat</b> is book eleven in <i>The Dresden Files</i> series by Jim Butcher.<br/><br/>Hot Dame what a start. Warden Morgan is in trouble; suspected of treason against the Wizarding Council and he turns to Harry for help. <br/><br/>If you’ve been reading this series you know Harry and Morgan don’t get along and also that Morgan is dedicated to the White Council, his job as a Warden, and a stickler for the rules. Harry would love to turn him in, but he knows that Morgan would never break the Laws of Magic.<br/><br/>Things just got mor</span>
  <span id="freeText14352740202561895577" style="display:none"><b>Turn Coat</b> is book eleven in <i>The Dresden Files</i> series by Jim Butcher.<br><br>Hot Dame what a start. Warden Morgan is in trouble; suspected of treason against the Wizarding Council and he turns to Harry for help. <br><br>If you’ve been reading this series you know Harry and Morgan don’t get along and also that Morgan is dedicated to the White Council, his job as a Warden, and a stickler for the rules. Harry would love to turn him in, but he knows that Morgan would never break the Laws of Magic.<br><br>Things just got more harry… He’s got two days to find the traitor in the White Council. After that Morgan and anyone that helped him goes down for the crime. Things get complicated fast. Friends and family get hurt and no one will be the same after it’s all done. <br><br>I enjoyed seeing Waldo Butters the medical examiner again. I adore and love Harry’s dog Mouse. Then we have Molly, Murphy, and Thomas. Each character grows on you and to see something happen to them that will change things; is good and also sad. Things with Thomas after this installment won’t be the same and we don’t know where Harry and him stand. I cried a little and was proud that Harry still says he’s his brother no mater what.<br><br><b>
  <i>Turn Coat</i>
</b> has no shortage of suspense, surprises, lose, and more. The Dresden Files is an extraordinary Urban Fantasy series. I can’t wait to see what’s next for Harry and the gang. <br><br><b>Rated: 5 Stars</b><br><br><a href="http://angelsguiltypleasures.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer3447438802769799611">I was planning on quitting this series if this one didn't measure up. Looks like I'm sticking around.<br/><br/>Morgan shows up at Harry's house with the Wardens on his trail, framed for murder. Harry goes about trying to clear Morgan's name, all the while dealing with a summoner named Binder and a demon called the Skinwalker.   <span id="freeText3447438802769799611" style="display:none">I was planning on quitting this series if this one didn't measure up. Harry goes about trying to clear Morgan's name, all the while dealing with a summoner named Binder and a demon called the Skinwalker. The plot advances.<br /><br />I can't imagine how anyone who has stuck out the series so far would find anything wrong with this one.         rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5514934369964391346">8/10<br/><br/>I’ll just look through my previous Dresden reviews and copy and paste it here. I’m running out of things to say on this series now that would provide anything new or insightful (not that I previously did provide those things anyway). <br/><br/>This was as good as the previous few novels keeping up what the series is good at; mysterious plot needing Harry to do some detective work whilst maintaining an ability to throw some quips around and using the assistance of those characters he’s previously been </span>
  <span id="freeText5514934369964391346" style="display:none">8/10<br /><br />I’ll just look through my previous Dresden reviews and copy and paste it here. I’m running out of things to say on this series now that would provide anything new or insightful (not that I previously did provide those things anyway). <br /><br />This was as good as the previous few novels keeping up what the series is good at; mysterious plot needing Harry to do some detective work whilst maintaining an ability to throw some quips around and using the assistance of those characters he’s previously been able to call upon. The added bonus this time is that there is more emphasis on the Black Council and their ability to weave closer to the White Council without their knowledge. Also, bonus points for EDINBURGH!! <br /><br />I enjoyed reading this, probably helped by the complete contrast in writing style and pacing to my previous book, A Storm of Swords, as things get going pretty quick and don’t really let off the pace until the very end. There are some good bad guys (with shocking names - Shagnasty?!) and the whole prospect of Harry having to work out a way to clear Morgan of murder when he has had nothing but run in’s with the douche previously was a nice touch.<br /><br />The ending was done nicely with enough resolution of certain things to feel like a satisfactory ending but with plenty of open threads still to be worked out in future novels. The Black Council thread is hotting up now and I’m keen to see where that leads and also to see <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ what the hell is going to happen with Thomas! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. A solid entry into the series leaving me wanting more. Solid Dresden win.<br /><br />If you like this try: “Going Postal” by Terry Pratchett</span>

<div id="review_2220150249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2220150249" />
    <a title="Juli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38617426-juli"><img alt="Juli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453642808p2/38617426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2220150249?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juli" href="/user/show/38617426-juli">Juli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781101052983" href="/book/show/7698424-turn-coat">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=read-off-my-shelves-2018">read-off-my-shelves-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=backlist-read-2018">backlist-read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2220150249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14178287187696318088">My husband loves The Dresden Files series. He's read every book and every short story. I'm trying to catch up with him so that we can enjoy the next book together. There is no publication date yet for Peace Talks -- book #16 -- so I have a bit of time to catch up while Jim Butcher finishes writing it. I'm trying to hurry though. My husband has a habit of blurting out major plot points ..... so I'm trying to get through the last book without him accidentally giving me any spoilers. <br/><br/>After enjoying</span>
  <span id="freeText14178287187696318088" style="display:none">My husband loves The Dresden Files series. He's read every book and every short story. I'm trying to catch up with him so that we can enjoy the next book together. There is no publication date yet for Peace Talks -- book #16 -- so I have a bit of time to catch up while Jim Butcher finishes writing it. I'm trying to hurry though. My husband has a habit of blurting out major plot points ..... so I'm trying to get through the last book without him accidentally giving me any spoilers. <br /><br />After enjoying the audio book for book #10 in the series, Small Favor, so much....I went with the audio version on this book, too. James Marsters narrates. He was great as Spike in Buffy.....and he's wonderful as Harry Dresden, too! He reads at a nice even pace and does all the character voices perfectly. Loved it! <br /><br />In Turn Coat, White Council Warden Morgan is wanted for murder.....he was found standing over the dead body of another council member, the murder weapon still in his hand. But he shows up on Dresden's doorstep saying that he didn't do it and asking for help. In the past, Morgan has tried to have Harry executed...and they just don't get along. But helping an innocent man is always the right thing....so Harry agrees. And once again he's almost instantly up to his eyeballs in danger. Another great action-packed urban fantasy story! This series never lets me down!<br /><br />Turn Coat is the 11th book in The Dresden Files. The series currently has 15 books, with the 16th book, Peace Talks, currently in progress. I'm moving on to book #12, Changes!<br /><br />I definitely recommend this series to anyone who enjoys urban fantasy. For me, the Dresden series is second only to Simon Green's Nightside books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14178287187696318088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_126524799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126524799" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126524799?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=ridiculously-prolific-authors">ridiculously-prolific-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=i-vant-to-drink-your-blood">i-vant-to-drink-your-blood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126524799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8565823636514413304"><b>Re-read Review, February 2018</b>: As with almost every book in this series, I liked it better this time. I've said this before, but there are advantages to reading the hard copies of the books, as much as I love the audio versions with James Marsters. And one of those advantages is it just takes so much less time to read a physical book, and stuff that you're not enjoying either goes faster or you can skip it outright. I remember when I read this book the first time it just felt a little too long, </span>
  <span id="freeText8565823636514413304" style="display:none"><b>Re-read Review, February 2018</b>: As with almost every book in this series, I liked it better this time. I've said this before, but there are advantages to reading the hard copies of the books, as much as I love the audio versions with James Marsters. And one of those advantages is it just takes so much less time to read a physical book, and stuff that you're not enjoying either goes faster or you can skip it outright. I remember when I read this book the first time it just felt a little too long, a little to dragged out. But this time it didn't feel like that at all. I think I must have re-read it in about two days. <br /><br />I also felt differently about Morgan this time around. The first time, I just couldn't get over how much of a shithead that guy was. How he was accepting help from Harry, which risked everyone in Harry's life, and he was STILL treating him (and Molly) with disdain. But the second time through, I could see that a lot of it was stubbornness, and he did see that. At the end, it's pretty clear that he believes in Harry enough to sacrifice his life to save him, and enough not to tell the Council about Molly relapsing a teensy bit into warlockian behavior. <br /><br />Plus, Butcher shoehorns in so much other cool stuff. Harry claiming Demonreach as sanctuary. The team-up with the Wraiths (who are terrifying). Finally some acknowledgement from Harry that the werewolves are adults now. And the monster. Oh, man, I'm not usually a fan of monster plots, but this one was genuinely terrifying. And even if I don't *like* it, I think Butcher deploys what the monster does to Thomas in an effective way.<br /><br />All in all, one of the best books of the series, and probably in the top two of the first half (pre-<i>Changes</i>, when everything, well, changes).<br /><br /><b>Original Review, May 2013</b>: I'm going to keep this (relatively) short because I'm about 7 gajillion reviews behind, but this series just keeps getting better and better. There aren't many series that I've read that up the ante like this as they go along. In fact, most start out really promising and then totally biff it along the way. The Dresden Files just keeps getting more interesting and exciting and emotionally complex. I think a lot of that might have something do with Butcher having started this series as a formulaic urban fantasy noir, but he's taken it to another place in the decade plus since. It's definitely not 'epic fantasy' but once might choose to use the phrase EPIC when describing it, if only because starting a new Dresden book lately makes me want to get on the floor and roll around and maybe squeal for a little bit.<br /><br /><i>Turn Coat</i> is the culmination of the series-long feud between Harry and the Warden known as Donald Morgan, a hundred year old wizard who is also the de facto executioner for the White Council, and who's had it out for Harry ever since he was sixteen years old. But this time, Morgan's in trouble. He's being framed for the murder of a member of the senior council, a murder which would also implicate him as a traitor, and he wants Harry's help to find the real murderer. Why Harry? Because Morgan knows Harry has experience in being unjustly vilified, and also he would literally rather die than see an innocent man condemned. And yes, the irony in this situation is delicious, for Harry and for us as readers. On top of that whole situation, Harry is being chased by a scary-ass monster called a Skinwalker, and his involvement in the case threatens not only his own safety, but that of his friends and family.<br /><br />I didn't like this one as much as I liked <i>Small Favor</i> or as much as I'm liking <i>Changes</i>, but it's pretty damn good. Morgan has always been a frustrating character for me, and he remained so for most of this book, but his arc wraps up nicely by the end. The flavor and intensity of the plot movement in this book hints that big stuff is coming, and Harry takes some pretty significant losses. The fact that these losses seem to largely be foreshadowing is a frightening thought. (And if some of them don't get, um, <i>fixed</i>, I'm going to throw a shit fit.)<br /><br />On to book twelve.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8565823636514413304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2954798830264347925" style="display:none">The darkest Dresden book by far. Morgan, a Warder of The White Court is framed for a murder of a fellow wizard. He is hunted to be executed on the spot. The only person who can possibly help him is happened to be Dresden. Yes, that same Dresden whom Morgan was intimidating for a long time trying to catch him doing black magic. As soon as Harry Dresden takes the case, a lot of powers come into play, including a few demigods - all against a poor Chicago's wizard PI. <br /><br />This is also probably the first book which cannot be considered to have a conclusion; it ends with a minor cliffhanger. <div id="review_84968070" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84968070" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/163750-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189653481p2/163750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84968070?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/163750-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=mystery-contemp-american">mystery-contemp-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=vampires-after-all">vampires-after-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163750-nicole?shelf=con-artists">con-artists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer84968070&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84968070" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer979819243993152367">First read 5-14 August, 2010. Re-read 8-28 May, 2012.<br/><br/>The carnage level was rather high, and the damage inflicted by the skinwalker and White Court was quite grisly. At least it wasn't all for shock value; there was some emotional punch to it. On the second reading, I found my eyes getting misty a few times. <br/>This installment of Harry's adventures hit the ground running and covered a lot of ground. It's dark but surprisingly good. Lots of bad things happening everywhere, but lots of heroism; and i</span>
  <span id="freeText979819243993152367" style="display:none">First read 5-14 August, 2010. Re-read 8-28 May, 2012.<br /><br />The carnage level was rather high, and the damage inflicted by the skinwalker and White Court was quite grisly. At least it wasn't all for shock value; there was some emotional punch to it. On the second reading, I found my eyes getting misty a few times. <br />This installment of Harry's adventures hit the ground running and covered a lot of ground. It's dark but surprisingly good. Lots of bad things happening everywhere, but lots of heroism; and it's put together in a way I've got to respect. Accumulating peril, double-crosses, stunning revelations, serious injuries--both physical and emotional--to Our Hero and others around him, some resolutions but also a set-up to even more of a thorny mess. Wow.<br />Poor Thomas. It was inevitable something would happen to impede his progress or ruin him altogether. What happened was awful, and I felt bad for him, Harry, and the other victims. But there's a glimmer of hope left.<br />All the things that had been bugging me about Warden Anastasia Luccio were explained. I didn't expect those twists the first time; and the second time, the situation still left me feeling melancholy.<br />Listens-to-Wind's display of transformation skills never gets old. What a throw-down with the skinwalker! Though I have to wonder if the creature will return, given the result of the fight. (I wish he'd just killed it.)<br />Mouse continued to charm. Some of the things he did in this book were priceless. And I liked the Senior Council's reaction to him.<br />I enjoyed seeing Ebenezar, Will, Georgia, and Toot-Toot (he certainly earned his promotion) again, as always.<br />RIP, Warden Donald Morgan. What a character. Cheers to Harry and Molly for trying to help, especially when Morgan himself didn't make it easy. In the end, Morgan did what had to be done and paid a huge price for it; and for that, I'm sad. The Council politics were just appalling.<br /><br />BTW...I have read a few reviews both by female and male readers who think that Harry is a chauvinist. I must respectfully disagree. I just don't see that, and I'm touchy about women being treated as inferior. I don't see Harry acting like the man in my office who treats almost everything women say as mildly amusing and generally incorrect. Two of Harry's strongest, most trusted allies are female. Harry knows he is not the most powerful, smartest guy in the world and he asks for help when he needs it, often from female characters.<br />I do have to admit that I sometimes roll my eyes at the number of hot chicks described in the series; but, as a male friend has reminded me, guys do view the world differently. Fiction doesn't tend to be chock-full of uglies, anyway. The vast majority of female characters in the series are not there simply as window dressing; they have skills. Plus, of the four women Harry has been most interested in, three were not described as super-hot-model types, and the one who was got vamped and her prettiness reduced considerably. Overall, the Dresden world seems pretty well-rounded to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="979819243993152367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2+rJiMPCTpM6b+J7kUHN5IghU96lJ8RuhYfqeneJDmEes+93cm44/ule828bKKvAHcJMNfi/Au+Nh8BYWDG79Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('65M8Kozdqikmvodjx0rbpnuwHM/m8JviOPKkS3DTmr8uyhrVPXHcRPWPlndNI72C7lMDJLtoXWMw8o5pX2svKw==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer9143703888342343990">Jim Butcher is the author of the Dresden Files, the Codex Alera, and a new steampunk series, the Cinder Spires. His resume includes a laundry list of skills which were useful a couple of centuries ago, and he plays guitar quite badly.   <span id="freeText9143703888342343990" style="display:none">Jim Butcher is the author of the Dresden Files, the Codex Alera, and a new steampunk series, the Cinder Spires. His resume includes a laundry list of skills which were useful a couple of centuries ago, and he plays guitar quite badly. An avid gamer, he plays tabletop games in varying systems, a variety of video games on PC and console, and LARPs whenever he can make time for it. Jim currently resides mostly inside his own head, but his head can generally be found in his home town of Independence, Missouri.<br /><br />Jim goes by the moniker Longshot in a number of online locales. He came by this name in the early 1990′s when he decided he would become a published author. Usually only 3 in 1000 who make such an attempt actually manage to become published; of those, only 1 in 10 make enough money to call it a living. The sale of a second series was the breakthrough that let him beat the long odds against attaining a career as a novelist.<br /><br />All the same, he refuses to change his nickname.<br /></span>
